</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Engineering</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Engineering_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Engineering (disambiguation)">Engineering (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/350px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" width="350" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/525px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/700px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="760" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engine</a>, a major driver in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, underscores the importance of engineering in modern history. This <a href="/wiki/Beam_engine" title="Beam engine">beam engine</a> is on display in the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Madrid" title="Technical University of Madrid">Technical University of Madrid</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Engineering</b> is the application of <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">scientific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economic</a>, social, and practical <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> in order to <a href="/wiki/Invention" title="Invention">invent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Innovate" class="mw-redirect" title="Innovate">innovate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Design" title="Design">design</a>, build, <a href="/wiki/Maintenance,_repair,_and_operations" title="Maintenance, repair, and operations">maintain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering_research" title="Engineering research">research</a>, and improve <a href="/wiki/Structural_engineering" title="Structural engineering">structures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machine" title="Machine">machines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tool" title="Tool">tools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Systems_engineering" title="Systems engineering">systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Part_(system)" class="mw-redirect" title="Part (system)">components</a>, <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">materials</a>, <a href="/wiki/Process_(engineering)" title="Process (engineering)">processes</a>, solutions, and <a href="/wiki/Organizations" class="mw-redirect" title="Organizations">organizations</a>.</p>
<p>The discipline of engineering is extremely broad and encompasses a range of more specialized <a href="/wiki/List_of_engineering_branches" title="List of engineering branches">fields of engineering</a>, each with a more specific emphasis on particular areas of applied science, <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> and types of application.</p>
<p>The term <i>Engineering</i> is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>ingenium</i>, meaning "cleverness" and <i>ingeniare</i>, meaning "to contrive, devise".<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Engineers%27_Council_for_Professional_Development" title="American Engineers' Council for Professional Development">American Engineers' Council for Professional Development</a> (ECPD, the predecessor of <a href="/wiki/Accreditation_Board_for_Engineering_and_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Accreditation Board for Engineering and Technology">ABET</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-ABET_History_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABET_History-2">[2]</a></sup> has defined "engineering" as:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The creative application of scientific principles to design or develop structures, machines, apparatus, or manufacturing processes, or works utilizing them singly or in combination; or to construct or operate the same with full cognizance of their design; or to forecast their behavior under specific operating conditions; all as respects an intended function, economics of operation or safety to life and property.<sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Canons_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Canons-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_engineering" title="History of engineering">History of engineering</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG/220px-Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG/330px-Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG/440px-Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grondplan_citadel_Lille.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Relief map of the <a href="/wiki/Citadel_of_Lille" title="Citadel of Lille">Citadel of Lille</a>, designed in 1668 by <a href="/wiki/Vauban" class="mw-redirect" title="Vauban">Vauban</a>, the foremost military engineer of his age.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Engineering has existed since ancient times as humans devised fundamental inventions such as the wedge, lever, wheel and pulley. Each of these inventions is essentially consistent with the modern definition of engineering.</p>
<p>The term <i>engineering</i> is derived from the word <i>engineer</i>, which itself dates back to 1390 when an <i>engine'er</i> (literally, one who operates an <i>engine</i>) originally referred to "a constructor of military engines."<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In this context, now obsolete, an "engine" referred to a military machine, <i>i.e.</i>, a mechanical contraption used in war (for example, a <a href="/wiki/Catapult" title="Catapult">catapult</a>). Notable examples of the obsolete usage which have survived to the present day are military engineering corps, <i>e.g.</i>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">U.S. Army Corps of Engineers</a>.</p>
<p>The word "engine" itself is of even older origin, ultimately deriving from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>ingenium</i> (c. 1250), meaning "innate quality, especially mental power, hence a clever invention."<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later, as the design of civilian structures such as bridges and buildings matured as a technical discipline, the term <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineering</a><sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup> entered the lexicon as a way to distinguish between those specializing in the construction of such non-military projects and those involved in the older discipline of <a href="/wiki/Military_engineering" title="Military engineering">military engineering</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_era">Ancient era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pont_du_gard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pont_du_gard.jpg/220px-Pont_du_gard.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pont_du_gard.jpg/330px-Pont_du_gard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pont_du_gard.jpg/440px-Pont_du_gard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pont_du_gard.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Ancient Romans built <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(watercourse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aqueduct (watercourse)">aqueducts</a> to bring a steady supply of clean fresh water to cities and towns in the empire.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pharos_of_Alexandria" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharos of Alexandria">Pharos of Alexandria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_pyramids" title="Egyptian pyramids">pyramids</a> in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hanging_Gardens_of_Babylon" title="Hanging Gardens of Babylon">Hanging Gardens of Babylon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Acropolis_of_Athens" title="Acropolis of Athens">Acropolis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Parthenon" title="Parthenon">Parthenon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_aqueduct" title="Roman aqueduct">Roman aqueducts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Via_Appia" class="mw-redirect" title="Via Appia">Via Appia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teotihuac%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Teotihuacán">Teotihuacán</a> and the cities and pyramids of the <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inca" class="mw-redirect" title="Inca">Inca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztec</a> Empires, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brihadeeswarar_Temple" title="Brihadeeswarar Temple">Brihadeeswarar Temple</a> of <a href="/wiki/Thanjavur" title="Thanjavur">Thanjavur</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Indian_Temples&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Indian Temples (page does not exist)">Indian Temples</a>, among many others, stand as a testament to the ingenuity and skill of the ancient civil and military engineers.</p>
<p>The earliest civil engineer known by name is <a href="/wiki/Imhotep" title="Imhotep">Imhotep</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup> As one of the officials of the <a href="/wiki/Pharaoh" title="Pharaoh">Pharaoh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Djoser" title="Djoser">Djosèr</a>, he probably designed and supervised the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_of_Djoser" title="Pyramid of Djoser">Pyramid of Djoser</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Step_Pyramid" class="mw-redirect" title="Step Pyramid">Step Pyramid</a>) at <a href="/wiki/Saqqara" title="Saqqara">Saqqara</a> in <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Egypt" title="History of ancient Egypt">Egypt</a> around <a href="/wiki/27th_century_BC" title="27th century BC">2630</a>–<a href="/wiki/27th_century_BC" title="27th century BC">2611 BC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Barry_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barry-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a> developed machines in both civilian and military domains. The <a href="/wiki/Antikythera_mechanism" title="Antikythera mechanism">Antikythera mechanism</a>, the first known <a href="/wiki/Analog_computer" title="Analog computer">mechanical computer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and the mechanical <a href="/wiki/Archimedes#Discoveries_and_inventions" title="Archimedes">inventions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Archimedes" title="Archimedes">Archimedes</a> are examples of early mechanical engineering. Some of Archimedes' inventions as well as the Antikythera mechanism required sophisticated knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Differential_(mechanical_device)" title="Differential (mechanical device)">differential gearing</a> or <a href="/wiki/Epicyclic_gearing" title="Epicyclic gearing">epicyclic gearing</a>, two key principles in machine theory that helped design the <a href="/wiki/Gear_train" title="Gear train">gear trains</a> of the Industrial Revolution, and are still widely used today in diverse fields such as <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Automotive_engineering" title="Automotive engineering">automotive engineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chinese, Greek, Roman and Hungarian armies employed complex military machines and inventions such as <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> which was developed by the Greeks around the 4th century B.C.,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Trireme" title="Trireme">trireme</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ballista" title="Ballista">ballista</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Catapult" title="Catapult">catapult</a>. In the Middle Ages, the <a href="/wiki/Trebuchet" title="Trebuchet">trebuchet</a> was developed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_era">Renaissance era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Renaissance era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engine</a> was built in 1698 by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Savery" title="Thomas Savery">Thomas Savery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jenkins_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jenkins-12">[12]</a></sup> The development of this device gave rise to the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> in the coming decades, allowing for the beginnings of <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">mass production</a>.</p>
<p>With the rise of engineering as a <a href="/wiki/Profession" title="Profession">profession</a> in the 18th century, the term became more narrowly applied to fields in which mathematics and science were applied to these ends. Similarly, in addition to military and civil engineering, the fields then known as the <a href="/wiki/Mechanic_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanic arts">mechanic arts</a> became incorporated into engineering.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg/250px-International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg" width="250" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg/375px-International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg/500px-International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3319" data-file-height="2116" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:International_Space_Station_after_undocking_of_STS-132.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> represents a modern engineering challenge from many disciplines.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The inventions of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Newcomen" title="Thomas Newcomen">Thomas Newcomen</a> and the Scottish engineer <a href="/wiki/James_Watt" title="James Watt">James Watt</a> gave rise to modern <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a>. The development of specialized machines and <a href="/wiki/Machine_tool" title="Machine tool">machine tools</a> during the industrial revolution led to the rapid growth of mechanical engineering both in its birthplace <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Britain</a> and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg/250px-Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg/375px-Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg/500px-Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="597" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_Mars_Lander_in_testing_PIA01885.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Structural engineers investigating NASA's Mars-bound <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(spacecraft)" title="Phoenix (spacecraft)">Phoenix Mars Lander</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Smeaton" title="John Smeaton">John Smeaton</a> was the first self-proclaimed civil engineer and is often regarded as the "father" of <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineering</a>. He was an English <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineer" title="Civil engineer">civil engineer</a> responsible for the design of <a href="/wiki/Bridge" title="Bridge">bridges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbour">harbours</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">lighthouses</a>. He was also a capable <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanical engineer">mechanical engineer</a> and an eminent <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicist</a>. Smeaton designed the third <a href="/wiki/Eddystone_Lighthouse" title="Eddystone Lighthouse">Eddystone Lighthouse</a> (1755–59) where he pioneered the use of '<a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_lime" title="Hydraulic lime">hydraulic lime</a>' (a form of <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(masonry)" title="Mortar (masonry)">mortar</a> which will set under water) and developed a technique involving dovetailed blocks of granite in the building of the lighthouse. His lighthouse remained in use until 1877 and was dismantled and partially rebuilt at <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Hoe" title="Plymouth Hoe">Plymouth Hoe</a> where it is known as <a href="/wiki/Smeaton%27s_Tower" title="Smeaton's Tower">Smeaton's Tower</a>. He is important in the history, rediscovery of, and development of modern <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a>, because he identified the compositional requirements needed to obtain "hydraulicity" in lime; work which led ultimately to the invention of <a href="/wiki/Portland_cement" title="Portland cement">Portland cement</a>.</p>
<p>The United States census of 1850 listed the occupation of "engineer" for the first time with a count of 2,000.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> There were fewer than 50 engineering graduates in the U.S. before 1865. In 1870 there were a dozen U.S. mechanical engineering graduates, with that number increasing to 43 per year in 1875. In 1890 there were 6,000 engineers in civil, mining, mechanical and electrical.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>There was no chair of applied mechanism and applied mechanics established at Cambridge until 1875, and no chair of engineering at Oxford until 1907. Germany established technical universities earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The foundations of <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a> in the 1800s included the experiments of <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Volta" title="Alessandro Volta">Alessandro Volta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Faraday" title="Michael Faraday">Michael Faraday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georg_Ohm" title="Georg Ohm">Georg Ohm</a> and others and the invention of the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_telegraph" title="Electrical telegraph">electric telegraph</a> in 1816 and the <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a> in 1872. The theoretical work of <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Maxwell</a> (see: <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%27s_equations" title="Maxwell's equations">Maxwell's equations</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Hertz" title="Heinrich Hertz">Heinrich Hertz</a> in the late 19th century gave rise to the field of <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>. The later inventions of the <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_tube" title="Vacuum tube">vacuum tube</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">transistor</a> further accelerated the development of electronics to such an extent that electrical and electronics engineers currently outnumber their colleagues of any other engineering specialty.<sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">Chemical engineering</a> developed in the late nineteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup> Industrial scale manufacturing demanded new materials and new processes and by 1880 the need for large scale production of chemicals was such that a new industry was created, dedicated to the development and large scale manufacturing of chemicals in new industrial plants.<sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup> The role of the chemical engineer was the design of these chemical plants and processes.<sup id="cite_ref-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECPD_Definition_on_Britannica-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg/250px-FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg" width="250" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg/375px-FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg/500px-FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2315" data-file-height="1644" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FalkirkWheelSide_2004_SeanMcClean.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Falkirk_Wheel" title="Falkirk Wheel">Falkirk Wheel</a> in Scotland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aeronautical engineering deals with <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_design_process" title="Aircraft design process">aircraft design process</a> design while <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_engineering" title="Aerospace engineering">aerospace engineering</a> is a more modern term that expands the reach of the discipline by including <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a> design. Its origins can be traced back to the aviation pioneers around the start of the 20th century although the work of <a href="/wiki/Sir_George_Cayley" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir George Cayley">Sir George Cayley</a> has recently been dated as being from the last decade of the 18th century. Early knowledge of aeronautical engineering was largely empirical with some concepts and skills imported from other branches of engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-americana_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-americana-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a> in engineering (technically, <i>applied science and engineering</i>) awarded in the United States went to <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Willard_Gibbs" title="Josiah Willard Gibbs">Josiah Willard Gibbs</a> at <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a> in 1863; it was also the second PhD awarded in science in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Only a decade after the successful flights by the <a href="/wiki/Wright_brothers" title="Wright brothers">Wright brothers</a>, there was extensive development of aeronautical engineering through development of military aircraft that were used in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Meanwhile, research to provide fundamental background science continued by combining <a href="/wiki/Theoretical_physics" title="Theoretical physics">theoretical physics</a> with experiments.</p>
<p>In 1990, with the rise of <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computer</a> technology, the first <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_(computing)" title="Search engine (computing)">search engine</a> was built by <a href="/wiki/Computer_engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer engineer">computer engineer</a> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Emtage" title="Alan Emtage">Alan Emtage</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_branches_of_engineering">Main branches of engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Main branches of engineering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoover_dam_from_air.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Hoover_dam_from_air.jpg/250px-Hoover_dam_from_air.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Hoover_dam_from_air.jpg/375px-Hoover_dam_from_air.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Hoover_dam_from_air.jpg/500px-Hoover_dam_from_air.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>

<a href="/wiki/Hoover_Dam" title="Hoover Dam">Hoover Dam</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Engineering is a broad discipline which is often broken down into several sub-disciplines. These disciplines concern themselves with differing areas of engineering work. Although initially an engineer will usually be trained in a specific discipline, throughout an engineer's career the engineer may become multi-disciplined, having worked in several of the outlined areas. Engineering is often characterized as having four main branches:<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UK_Council_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Council-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramchandani2000_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramchandani2000-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">Chemical engineering</a> – The application of physics, chemistry, biology, and engineering principles in order to carry out chemical processes on a commercial scale, such as <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">petroleum refining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microfabrication" title="Microfabrication">microfabrication</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fermentation" title="Fermentation">fermentation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biomolecule production</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">Civil engineering</a> – The design and construction of public and private works, such as <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a> (<a href="/wiki/Airports" class="mw-redirect" title="Airports">airports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roads" class="mw-redirect" title="Roads">roads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Railways">railways</a>, water supply, and treatment etc.), <a href="/wiki/Bridge" title="Bridge">bridges</a>, dams, and buildings.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">Electrical engineering</a> – The design, study, and manufacture of various electrical and electronic systems, such as <a href="/wiki/Electrical_circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical circuit">electrical circuits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_generator" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical generator">generators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">motors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetism" title="Electromagnetism">electromagnetic</a>/<a href="/wiki/Electromechanical" class="mw-redirect" title="Electromechanical">electromechanical</a> devices, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_devices" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic devices">electronic devices</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_circuits" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic circuits">electronic circuits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">optical fibers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optoelectronic_device" class="mw-redirect" title="Optoelectronic device">optoelectronic devices</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computer</a> systems, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>, instrumentation, controls, and <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">Mechanical engineering</a> – The design and manufacture of physical or mechanical systems, such as power and <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> systems, <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a>/<a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a> products, <a href="/wiki/Weapon_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Weapon systems">weapon systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation">transportation</a> products, <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">engines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gas_compressor" title="Gas compressor">compressors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Powertrain" title="Powertrain">powertrains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kinematic_chain" title="Kinematic chain">kinematic chains</a>, vacuum technology, <a href="/wiki/Vibration_isolation" title="Vibration isolation">vibration isolation</a> equipment, <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mechatronics" title="Mechatronics">mechatronics</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Beyond these "Big Four", a number of other branches are recognized. Historically, <a href="/wiki/Naval_architecture" title="Naval architecture">naval engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mining_engineering" title="Mining engineering">mining engineering</a> were major branches. Other engineering fields sometimes included as major branches<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> are <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_engineering" title="Manufacturing engineering">manufacturing engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acoustical_engineering" title="Acoustical engineering">acoustical engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corrosion_engineering" title="Corrosion engineering">corrosion engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instrumentation_and_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Instrumentation and control">instrumentation and control</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_engineering" title="Aerospace engineering">aerospace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automotive_engineering" title="Automotive engineering">automotive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_engineering" title="Computer engineering">computer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_engineering" title="Electronic engineering">electronic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_engineering" title="Petroleum engineering">petroleum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_engineering" title="Environmental engineering">environmental</a>, <a href="/wiki/Systems_engineering" title="Systems engineering">systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audio_engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Audio engineering">audio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_engineering" title="Software engineering">software</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architectural_engineering" title="Architectural engineering">architectural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_engineering" title="Agricultural engineering">agricultural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biosystems_engineering" title="Biosystems engineering">biosystems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_engineering" title="Biomedical engineering">biomedical</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Geological_engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Geological engineering">geological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textile_manufacturing" title="Textile manufacturing">textile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_engineering" title="Industrial engineering">industrial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">materials</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_engineering" title="Nuclear engineering">nuclear</a> engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> These and other branches of engineering are represented in the 36 licensed member institutions of the UK <a href="/wiki/Engineering_Council" title="Engineering Council">Engineering Council</a>.</p>
<p>New specialties sometimes combine with the traditional fields and form new branches – for example, <a href="/wiki/Earth_systems_engineering_and_management" title="Earth systems engineering and management">Earth systems engineering and management</a> involves a wide range of subject areas including <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering_studies" title="Engineering studies">engineering studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_science" title="Environmental science">environmental science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">ethics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_engineering" title="Philosophy of engineering">philosophy of engineering</a>. A new or emerging area of application will commonly be defined temporarily as a permutation or subset of existing disciplines; there is often gray area as to when a given sub-field warrants classification as a new "branch." One key indicator of such emergence is when major universities start establishing departments and programs in the new field.</p>
<p>For each of these fields, there exists considerable overlap, especially in the areas of the application of fundamental sciences to their disciplines such as physics, chemistry, and mathematics. As a result, there are many different types of engineering degrees available. In the past, engineering could be divided into four major branches: mechanical, chemical, civil and electrical, with sub-branches of each discipline. Today, however, the number of engineering degrees available have increased dramatically.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Practice">Practice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Practice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One who practices engineering is called an <a href="/wiki/Engineer" title="Engineer">engineer</a>, and those licensed to do so may have more formal designations such as <a href="/wiki/Professional_Engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Professional Engineer">Professional Engineer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chartered_Engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chartered Engineer">Chartered Engineer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Incorporated_Engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Incorporated Engineer">Incorporated Engineer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ingenieur" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingenieur">Ingenieur</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Engineer" title="European Engineer">European Engineer</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration#Designated_Engineering_Representative_.28DER.29" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Designated Engineering Representative</a>. In the UK many trades are called "Engineer" including gas, telephone, photocopy, maintenance, plumber-heating, drainage, sanitary, auto mechanic, TV, Refrigerator, electrician, washing machine, TV antenna installer (satellite) and many others.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methodology">Methodology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Methodology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. </tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg/225px-Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg" width="225" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg/338px-Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg/450px-Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1779" data-file-height="2126" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dampfturbine_Montage01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Design of a <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">turbine</a> requires collaboration of engineers from many fields, as the system involves mechanical, electro-magnetic and chemical processes. The <a href="/wiki/Turbine_blade" title="Turbine blade">blades</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stator" title="Stator">rotor and stator</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Steam_cycle" class="mw-redirect" title="Steam cycle">steam cycle</a> all need to be carefully designed and optimized.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Engineers apply mathematics and sciences such as physics to find novel solutions to problems or to improve existing solutions. More than ever, engineers are now required to have a proficient knowledge of relevant sciences for their design projects. As a result, many engineers continue to learn new material throughout their career.</p>
<p>If multiple solutions exist, engineers weigh each design choice based on their merit and choose the solution that best matches the requirements. The crucial and unique task of the engineer is to identify, understand, and interpret the constraints on a design in order to yield a successful result. It is generally insufficient to build a technically successful product, rather, it must also meet further requirements.</p>
<p>Constraints may include available resources, physical, imaginative or technical limitations, flexibility for future modifications and additions, and other factors, such as requirements for cost, <a href="/wiki/Safety_engineering" title="Safety engineering">safety</a>, marketability, productivity, and <a href="/wiki/Serviceability_(computer)" title="Serviceability (computer)">serviceability</a>. By understanding the constraints, engineers derive <a href="/wiki/Specifications" class="mw-redirect" title="Specifications">specifications</a> for the limits within which a viable object or system may be produced and operated.</p>
<p>A general methodology and <a href="/wiki/Epistemology" title="Epistemology">epistemology</a> of engineering can be inferred from the historical case studies and comments provided by Walter Vincenti.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Though Vincenti's case studies are from the domain of aeronautical engineering, his conclusions can be transferred into many other branches of engineering, too.</p>
<p>According to Billy Vaughn Koen, the "<i>engineering method</i> is the use of heuristics to cause the best change in a poorly understood situation within the available resources." Koen argues that the definition of what makes one an engineer should not be based on what he produces, but rather how he goes about it.<sup id="cite_ref-Discussion_of_The_Method_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Discussion_of_The_Method-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Problem_solving">Problem solving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Problem solving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Engineering&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
